  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c9e7345a-c5ba-462a-878e-41ed947587c6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It didn't remind me of either series because they are all so very different. The main thing that I think they have in common is that they are so well <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">â¦more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It didn't remind me of either series because they are all so very different. The main thing that I think they have in common is that they are so well written. As I read each of these books I could always visualise what was happening so very vividly. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_757131753" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/757131753" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757131753?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757131753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10989574048418810098">DNF at 25%. I have theories about what happens throughout the rest of the book. Read my theories at the end, those who have read this series, and tell me if I'm wrong.<br/><br/>I fully expected to enjoy this book, or at least find plenty of entertainment value, given that it was written by Julie Kagawa.<br/><br/><b>I was wrong.</b><br/><br/>Last week I read the fantastically craptastic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471493023?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Firelight</a> which was essentially <i>Twilight</i> with dragons. So my standards weren't high to begin with. This book was only marginally better, and only so</span>
  <span id="freeText10989574048418810098" style="display:none">DNF at 25%. I have theories about what happens throughout the rest of the book. Read my theories at the end, those who have read this series, and tell me if I'm wrong.<br /><br />I fully expected to enjoy this book, or at least find plenty of entertainment value, given that it was written by Julie Kagawa.<br /><br /><b>I was wrong.</b><br /><br />Last week I read the fantastically craptastic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471493023?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Firelight</a> which was essentially <i>Twilight</i> with dragons. So my standards weren't high to begin with. This book was only marginally better, and only so due to Kagawa's writing.<br /><br />Kagawa is a writer whose works I enjoy. Fuck, I <i>liked</i> the much-reviled and oftentimes stupid Meghan in the <i>Iron Fey</i> series, I overlooked the tragic love triangle, because those books were <i>fun</i>. Not so with this one.<br /><br /><b>I could tell from the first few chapters that this wouldn't be a book I enjoyed, and the fact is reinforced throughout the story.</b> Dragons are cool. Dragons are deadly. They breathe fire, they kill people, they're awesome! I wanted a main character like that. Instead, I got <b>a main character who's a dragon but really just wanted to fit in with the humans.</b> There is literally no distinguishing her from every other rebellious teenager ever besides for the fact that she can turn into a dragon. She's rebellious! She wants freedom! She wants to go to the beach and chill and have friends, yo. So badass. Not.<blockquote>
  <i>I was tired of rules and isolation, of watching the world go by without me. I was tired of Talon and their endless string of policies, laws and restrictions. No more of that. The summer was mine, and I had big plans, things I wanted to do, before it ended and weâd be forced back into the system. This summer, I was going to live.</i>
</blockquote><b>There is nothing original about the main character that would make her different from every other Mary Sue in existence.</b> For example, she is one of a super super rare couple of dragon twins, and besides, she's designed to be physically stunning.<blockquote>
  <i>When choosing the form that would be ours for the rest of our life, everyone in Talon was groomed to the highest standards of human beauty.</i>
</blockquote>Fuck that shit. I don't want a stunning human girl, I want a bad-ass fire-breathing, ass-kicking, princess-eating dragon.<br /><br />And then, for fuck's sakes, there's the whole <b>OH MY GOD THIS CRAZY MYSTERIOUS AND HANDSOME BOY HAS NEVER LOOKED AT ANYONE BEFORE BUT THAT'S BECAUSE HE'S ONLY BEEN WAITING FOR YOU.</b><blockquote>
  <i>âGorgeous Biker Boy,â Lexi replied as the strange dragon continued to stare at me, almost challenging. âNo one knows who he is. He showed up a few weeks ago, and has been coming around all the popular hangouts. He never talks to anyone, just checks the place out, like heâs looking for somebody, and leaves.â Her knee bumped mine under the table, making me jump, and she grinned wickedly. âBut it seems like heâs found what he was looking for.â</i>
</blockquote>âGorgeous Biker Boy,â Lexi replied as the strange dragon continued to stare at me, almost challenging. âNo one knows who he is. He showed up a few weeks ago, and has been coming around all the popular hangouts. He never talks to anyone, just checks the place out, like heâs looking for somebody, and leaves.â Her knee bumped mine under the table, making me jump, and she grinned wickedly. âBut it seems like heâs found what he was looking for.âAnd then there's the <b>insta-love</b>. Come on, now!<blockquote>
  <i>But I remembered the strange dragonâs eyes, the look on his face as heâd stared at me, the way my blood had warmed at the sight of him. I remembered the heat of his gaze, the instant awakening of something fierce and primal inside me when our eyes met.<br />The rogue dragon was trouble. Plain and simple.<br />And I was intrigued.</i>
</blockquote><b>All of that idiocy is uncovered within the first few chapters.</b> And I have a clear idea of how things are going to go.<br /><br />From her rebellious and not-so-charming-free-spiritedness, I'm going to guess that Ember <b>constantly does stupid shit to put herself in danger.</b> Like changing into human and back into dragon form because it's so important that the dragons keep their existence a secret.<blockquote>
  <i>The art of Shiftingâchanging into human formâwas so widespread it was common dragon knowledge now. All our kind knew how to do it. And those that couldnât were either taught very quickly, or they were hunted down by the Order of St. George, the terrible cult of dragonslayers whose only purpose was our destruction. Shifting into human form was our best defense against genocidal dragon killers and a world of unsuspecting mortals; one did not just wander about in full reptile form unless one had a death wish.</i>
</blockquote>I'm going to guess that she flouts the rules every chance she gets. I'm going to guess that there's a love triangle, involving that gorgeous forbidden dragon from the quote above, and someone else. That other someone will either be her long-lost friend or an enemy whose purpose is to kill her, Ã  la <i>Firelight</i>. Am I wrong?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4943751849290043311">Could this really be the same author who wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_' title='The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron King</a>?<br/><br/>Never have I heard of dragons being boring. Until this.<br/><br/>Where is the <strong>incredible</strong> world-building? The <strong>originality</strong> in characters? The <strong>exciting</strong> romance?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413086709ra/11464241.gif' width='300' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I would like to know. Have you read the blurb? The blurb which promises us so muchâ¦yet the story does not deliver. And it is disappointing! To tell you everything, the only reason I have not DNFed this is because I just DNFed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_' title='These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman' rel='nofollow noopener'>These Broken Stars</a> yesterday and would have feltâ¦cheap to do so wi</span>
  <span id="freeText4943751849290043311" style="display:none">Could this really be the same author who wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron King</a>?<br><br>Never have I heard of dragons being boring. Until this.<br><br>Where is the <strong>incredible</strong> world-building? The <strong>originality</strong> in characters? The <strong>exciting</strong> romance?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413086709ra/11464241.gif" width="300" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would like to know. Have you read the blurb? The blurb which promises us so muchâ¦yet the story does not deliver. And it is disappointing! To tell you everything, the only reason I have not DNFed this is because I just DNFed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_" title="These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">These Broken Stars</a> yesterday and would have feltâ¦cheap to do so with this one as well. So I struggled to read it but did skim here and there. And, at the end, felt like Iâve lost six hours forâ¦nothing.<br><br>What I really didnât like is seeing how this had nothing outstanding. Thereâs everything you might think there would be, no surprises. There are dragonsâ¦and, of course, dragon slayers. Thereâs this main character around whom the plot turns. She is important and special and everyone is after her. There would be barely any story without her. There are those superficial secondary characters that only think of boys. Which brings me toâ¦.<br><br>The love-triangle. The awful, unnecessary and annoying love-triangle. Why do authors think we, teenagers, love those so much? Because we donât. I may not always mind them and it can happen that I enjoy them when theyâre not predictable and boring but, really, everything is better off without them. So the romance was definitely a weakness to the story, while it should have been the contrary.<br><br>Ember was the banal kind of heroine you can find in every other YA book. I think, with her being a dragon, the author wanted to make her seem original and spectacular but, really, sheâs just plain unimpressive. The main problem though is that<strong> sheâs supposed to be a dragon first and a human second</strong>. And she was not. I can barely believe, even now, that sheâs in reality a dragon. I really liked her twin brother though. There wasnât that much of him but, when he was present, I enjoyed reading about him.<br><br>The writing was quite good. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a> knows<em> how</em> to write a story. But, this time, <em>what she wrote</em> about was not appealing. The dialogs felt real, but they were usually not bringing or developing an interesting subject to know about. It mostly was normal conversation or the type that felt âobligatoryâ in the chapter or context.<br><br>So, Iâm giving this two stars but, unfortunately, I feel a little generous about it. Basically, it is well-written, has a crappy romance, uninteresting characters (except for DanteâEmberâs brother,) a plot that is predictable and lacks of surprises and dragons that will leave youâ¦emotionless.<br><br>Not recommended, except if youâre a die-hard fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2995873.Julie_Kagawa" title="Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Kagawa</a> and <em>love</em> everything she writes.</span>

<div id="review_553929816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/553929816" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553929816?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553929816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10700852305409556873">I just... can't... finish it. <br/><br/>I tried, really I did. I'm a big fan of Kagawa's work and I've enjoyed both her Fae books and her vampire trilogy; it was only natural that I was dying to get my hands on her brand new series about <b>dragons who take human form</b>.<br/><br/>But there was a missing spark for me that I managed to find in her other two series. Plus, throw in a bunch of regular YA paranormal cliches like a love triangle and this book, despite the original-sounding premise, was nothing special. You can</span>
  <span id="freeText10700852305409556873" style="display:none">I just... can't... finish it. <br /><br />I tried, really I did. I'm a big fan of Kagawa's work and I've enjoyed both her Fae books and her vampire trilogy; it was only natural that I was dying to get my hands on her brand new series about <b>dragons who take human form</b>.<br /><br />But there was a missing spark for me that I managed to find in her other two series. Plus, throw in a bunch of regular YA paranormal cliches like a love triangle and this book, despite the original-sounding premise, was nothing special. You can tell almost immediately who the love interest is going to be, just from the description of his badass smirk.<br /><br />And it wasn't even the cliches and transparent plot line. Kagawa's other books aren't exactly dazzling with originality, but they are compulsively readable and addictive. They move along at a pace that demands to be read. They introduce us to characters that interest, intrigue and piss us off.<br /><br />It's possible that I took too long to read <i>Talon</i>. I've had less time lately and maybe the constant putting it down and picking it up made it difficult for me to become fully invested in the story, but I'm not going to waste any more of my precious reading time on a book that isn't doing it for me. As always, if positive reviews roll in, I might try again.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.leafmarks.com/emilymay" rel="nofollow noopener">Leafmarks</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_556835822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Steysha Kravits" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9946057-steysha-kravits"><img alt="Steysha Kravits" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470471485p2/9946057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/556835822?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steysha Kravits" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steysha Kravits" href="/user/show/9946057-steysha-kravits">Steysha Kravits</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556835822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer987735977043952042">What I expected:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406081542ra/10500430.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>What I got:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/653064.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love Julie Kagawa. Iâve read her Iron Fey series and I liked it. So I had great expectations upon this book. I meanâ¦ itâs about dragons! But Iâm actually disappointed.<br/><br/>Ember and her twin Dante are exceptional. Dragons usually lay only one egg a time, so they donât have siblings. They live in a Talon â organization that helps them to survive in a world, where dragons are killed by St. George â military forces, created to drive dragons to extinct. <br/>Ember and Dante are su</span>
  <span id="freeText987735977043952042" style="display:none">What I expected:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406081542ra/10500430.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>What I got:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/653064.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Julie Kagawa. Iâve read her Iron Fey series and I liked it. So I had great expectations upon this book. I meanâ¦ itâs about dragons! But Iâm actually disappointed.<br><br>Ember and her twin Dante are exceptional. Dragons usually lay only one egg a time, so they donât have siblings. They live in a Talon â organization that helps them to survive in a world, where dragons are killed by St. George â military forces, created to drive dragons to extinct. <br>Ember and Dante are supposed to learn how to assimilate with humans during their summer in California, while training to become actual members of Talon and start to work for the organization. But Ember doesnât want to work â she wants to have fun with her friends, go surfing and do pretty much nothing. <br>Then she meets a rogue dragon that puts under question all she knew before, and falls in love with a boy, which is strictly forbidden and unnatural for a dragon. And yes, ladies and gentlemen, we have a love triangle. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409993191ra/11050858.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ember is soooo annoying. Sheâs whiny, childish and irresponsible. I felt like I was reading about a 10-year-old. All she does is rambles about how bad is Talon, because they make her listen to the rules and train her to become a real dragon, while she wants to go for a walk with her friends. <br>For example, she instantly thinks her trainer is a Bitch, because she teaches her how to fight St. George when our girl dreams about boys, and never pats her shoulder when she does something good (which isnât often). She isnât your loving mother, moron, she trains you how to survive in a world where dragons are killed! <br><br><b>
  <i>Which was why I had so been looking forward to the summer, one final hurrah before I had to become a responsible member of the organization. Before I became a full member of Talon for life, which was a very, very long time for us. Three months, that was all I wanted. Was that too much to ask?</i>
</b><br><br>Um, let me get this straight. She trains in the morning. That she can do whatever she wants. She has a lot of time for surfing, shopping and for going out with her friends. But she never. Stops. Whining. <br><br>Moreover, it gets her a lot of time for doing stupid things. Her brother asked her repeatedly not to bend the rules, because if Talon finds out, theyâll be sent back. This is their only chance to prove themselves. Pfff, like this girl cares. Sheâs attracted by everything that is forbidden: hang out with a rogue? Check. Turn into a dragon? Check. Get attached to humans? Check. <br><br>The story was also predictable from the very start. We knew that Garret is from the St. George, and maybe thatâs the reason why every time Ember met with him it looked obvious to me. But seriously: this guy has never heard about arcade, he has no friends, everything is new to him, as itâs for Ember. But that doesnât ring a bell, for he seems perfectly normal to her. Garret also shows her that he is good at combat and that heâs a perfect shooter. But the girl doesnât even ask where he learned it. For a dragon who all her life was taught that St. George is after them, sheâs incredibly oblivious. All she cares about is for her feelings for him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396994868ra/9215943.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, this book is cheesy and full of clichÃ©s. Like the part where Ember and her friends met some strangers and decided to ride with them to a cave. As Ember thought, these guys were looking âfor funâ. Then girls are saved from those rapists by a knight in shining armor, and guess what? It taught them nothing, they sat in the car with another stranger and immediately invited him to a party in the house of one of the girls. What the hell??? You donât even know him! <br>I remember watching some documental film about dinosaurs, and there was a scene where one tyrannosaur killed another, so that he could leave its prey for himself. You get it, Ember?<br><br>The girl also does this strange thing when she talks about herself as a dragon and herself as a human, like they are two different persons. For instance, she-human liked Garret, while she-dragon bristled at the thought of him. Sounds like she has a split personality.<br><br>There were three POVs, Ember`s, Garret`s and Riley`s â the rogue dragon. And while I was annoyed by Ember, boys were actually good, if you donât count their endless praises for her when she doesnât deserve it. <br><br>The writing was good, I liked the battle scenes, it was epic. Also I loved the description of Kagawa`s dragons, it was pretty realistic. I mean:<br><br><b>
  <i>Something dark, scaly, and massive erupted from the hacienda, sending tile and wood flying as it launched itself into the air. My heart jumped as I watched the monster soar above the canopy. It was huge, a full-grown adult, the height of a bull elephant and three times as long. Curved horns spiraled up from its narrow skull, and a mane of spines ran down its neck to a long, thrashing tail. The sun glinted off midnight scales, and leathery wings cast a long shadow over the ground as the dragon hovered in the air, glaring down at the battle below, then dove to attack.</i>
</b><br><br>The plot wasnât very interesting, because, as I said, it was predictable. The characters made me feel like banging my head against the wall, though I really liked Riley. Unfortunately, I expected much more. <b>2,5-3 stars.</b></span>

  <span id="freeText6670655095425000100" style="display:none"><b>well that was painfully average. </b><br /><br />I love Julie Kagawa. Truly, I do. Her Iron Fey series was once my favorite YA series. And of course, average inta-love with an average love triangle.<br /><br />This is the kind of book I feel that Iâve read before if only because of how uninspiring it was. There was nothing too original or intriguing about it. There was nothing memorable.<br /><br /><b>Overall, it was justâ¦meh.</b><br /><br />So, is it wrong that a small, strangely masochistic part of me kinda wants to continue this bland series? I suppose weâll see what happens. I might get desperate one of these days and pick up the sequel. But Talon didn't really have any of that - and I actually didn't mind. I still enjoyed reading this. And I have a feeling that there wi</span>
  <span id="freeText15785401352266934791" style="display:none"><b>Review:</b><br><br>I FINISHED IT. FINALLY. If you've read her Iron Fey series, or her Immortal Rules series, you'd know that adventure is a big part of the story. It's one of my favourite things about her books. But Talon didn't really have any of that - and I actually didn't mind. I still enjoyed reading this. And I have a feeling that there will be a lot of surprises in the next books in the series, so I'm really looking forward to that.<br><br>The characters - gah, I loved them all! Ember did seem a bit immature at first, but I still liked her. Garrett was awesome. I loved reading in his point of view. And Riley...okay, I love Garrett, and I know that Riley probably won't end up with Ember, but goddammit I want him to! <br><br>The romance was so sweet. Ember and Garrett's attraction towards each other did seem a bit too sudden, but the more I read abut them, the less I cared. They're just too cute together.<br><br>And...dragons, guys. DRAGONS. It has a slower pace and is set in the regular human world. It would be easy to become disappointed if you're expecting this series to be like her other works. I still loved it. It may seem like I'm biased towards JK, but had a feeling that this series would be different, and that I would read it with an open mind. So I hope you all give this book a chance.<br><br>So there you have it, guys. Julie Kagawa has done it again.     <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=unoriginal">unoriginal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=boooooring">boooooring</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646693341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9431270845868083617"><b>2.5</b> stars, as much as it pains me to do this.<br/><br/>Julie, oh Julie. Why you gotta do me like that? u_u<br/><br/>Prior to reading this book, I was like:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414770595ra/11689832.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Because it's <i>Julie</i>! I adore her to pieces. The <i>Iron Fey</i> series to date is one of my favorite series' of all time, and so is <i>Blood of Eden</i>. She put out constant masterpieces that, naturally, I put her on a pedestal.<br/><br/>After reading this book, I'm starting to think that was not a very wise idea. ._.<br/><br/><b>This book suffered a massive case of blandness.</b> It was extremely formu</span>
  <span id="freeText9431270845868083617" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b> stars, as much as it pains me to do this.<br><br>Julie, oh Julie. Why you gotta do me like that? u_u<br><br>Prior to reading this book, I was like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414770595ra/11689832.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because it's <i>Julie</i>! I adore her to pieces. The <i>Iron Fey</i> series to date is one of my favorite series' of all time, and so is <i>Blood of Eden</i>. She put out constant masterpieces that, naturally, I put her on a pedestal.<br><br>After reading this book, I'm starting to think that was not a very wise idea. ._.<br><br><b>This book suffered a massive case of blandness.</b> It was extremely formulaic and seemed like it didn't even try to get much originality in. I mean, granted, Julie's series' were never really <i>that</i> original either, but at least things actually happened in those books, and the characters were wonderful. <i>Talon</i>, however, just dragged and dragged, and the characters felt lifeless to me. Not to mention the plethora of cliches and age-old YA tropes.<br><br>And yet, I pressed on, because I kept telling myself, "This is <i>Julie effing Kagawa!</i> A new series! Squeeee, much?!" So I kept reading, hoping it'd improve down the road. I was all, "Come on, Julie, where's all that awesomeness you have in you? Don't tell me you've used it all up already!"<br><br>But the further I read, the more she was all,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414770595ra/11689833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There were sparks--so to speak--of Julie's magic in there, though.</b> It's not as if I completely hated the book or anything, because there were tiny bits I liked. But they were just that; tiny bits. Sparks. Most of the time it didn't even feel like this was her book, because I know for a fact that she can do <i>so much better</i>.<br><br>But the big question is, <b>do I still have hope for this series?</b><br><br>Well...<br><br>Fuck, I have no clue. On the one hand, yeah, it may end up being great. But on the other hand... I really don't care for these characters. &gt;_&lt; I mean what do you do with that, y'know? When you read the first book in a series and barely give a crap about the characters, how would you continue on with the sequels?<br><br>*sigh* I don't know, you guys. I'm just overwhelmed with crushing disappointment right now. I don't really wanna think about it yet. I'm just trying to convince myself that sometimes, people who are amazing at what they do, still stumble. That's exactly what happened here, but I still have a special place in my heart for Ms. Kagawa and have hope that she'll pull through.<br><br>This book is a big no-no, and yet there is still a 2% chance that I may end up continuing the series, regardless of my lack of care for the characters. It's just... It's Julie, goddammit! &gt;_&lt;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414770595ra/11689834.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1266057090" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266057090" />
    <a title="Kristina Horner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner"><img alt="Kristina Horner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425746408p2/3070540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266057090?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina Horner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina Horner" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner">Kristina Horner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266057090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer803717861342348325">Okay. I have seriously been looking forward to writing this review. Because I HATED Talon with every fiber of my being and can't even think of ONE redeeming quality, aside from perhaps the fact that my roommate and I had a joyous time bonding over our simultaneous hate-reads of this audiobook. Sometimes reading a bad book can be fun, I'll admit it. But other times, it can make you want to drive your car off a cliff as you BEAT YOUR HEAD AGAINST THE STEERING WHEEL BECAUSE EVERYONE IN THE BOOK IS </span>
  <span id="freeText803717861342348325" style="display:none">Okay. I have seriously been looking forward to writing this review. Because I HATED Talon with every fiber of my being and can't even think of ONE redeeming quality, aside from perhaps the fact that my roommate and I had a joyous time bonding over our simultaneous hate-reads of this audiobook. Sometimes reading a bad book can be fun, I'll admit it. But other times, it can make you want to drive your car off a cliff as you BEAT YOUR HEAD AGAINST THE STEERING WHEEL BECAUSE EVERYONE IN THE BOOK IS SO STUPID. <br><br>To back up - I got this book because it was an Audible daily deal, which meant it was $2. A fun YA romance about dragons pretending to be humans -- sounds at least entertaining, right? Definitely at least worth $2.<br><br>WRONG.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431131325ra/14794983.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First off, THEY'RE BARELY EVEN DRAGONS. THIS IS JUST A TERRIBLE CONTEMPORARY ROMANCE. They only seemed to remember they were dragons when it was convenient. "I don't understand human emotions," Ember says, instantly falling in love with literally the first human boy she meets even though its explicitly stated dragons don't love, all while effortlessly referencing NCIS. "I've been a rogue, living away from everything," Riley says, then proceeds to quote Shrek before insisting they need to "get the hell out of Dodge". "All I know is murder and killing and war," Garret says, insisting he's a hardcore soldier but also instantly falling in love with the girl/dragon he's supposed to kill, forgetting his life-long mission over a girl he like, played video games with once.<br><br>This book is about 2 dragons and a solider who are actually the worst 2 dragons and soldier that ever existed. All dragon and solider aspects of this book just get in the way of the messy, forced, unbelievable "romance" that Julie Kagawa has cobbled together and she fights it at every chance she gets, often contradicting parameters she set up earlier in the book about being a dragon. <br>Let me ask you something, Ms. Kagawa. IF YOU JUST WANTED TO WRITE A BAD LOVE TRIANGLE BETWEEN TEENAGERS, WHY DIDN'T YOU JUST MAKE THEM HUMAN TEENAGERS. I'M NOT BUYING THIS HALF-ASSED FANTASY STUFF. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431133134ra/14795142.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My roommate said he got through the book more easily pretending that these were people with mental disorders who just THOUGHT they were dragons. I tend to agree. That was a vast improvement.<br><br>There was so. much. repetitive. writing. If I had decided to drink every time someone ran a hand through their hair, I'd be dead. If I have to hear the phrase "looked up at him through my eyelashes" again, I will rage. And seriously, what does "scrubbing" your hands over something mean? Ember scrubbed her hands over literally everything. Her hair. Her eyes. Her face. Constantly. Why.<br><br>It made me so made that Riley kept teasing his ~secrets about Talon~ and I was really hoping for something shocking or bad because his whole schtick was "but I have ~secrets~ about your world" and then in the end it was just like "they're bad lol run away with me!". UGH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431133134ra/14795143.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NOTHING was logical. At all. From the fact that Ember's cunning human disguise was to be a red-headed human whose name LITERALLY TRANSLATES TO FIRE to the fact that the elite order of St. George sent two teenagers to pal around all summer with girls to find the "deadly dragon" rather than I dont know, <i>inventing some sort of way to test it</i> to the fact that Riley suddenly just decided he and Ember were going to be in love and carried this decision out in a super rapey way... ugh. Just ugh. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431133134ra/14795144.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wasn't expecting a good book out of Talon, honestly. I was expecting it to be silly, or at least fun in an eye-rolling sort of way. <br>But this pile of nonsense is so bad I can't even deal with the fact that I listened to the whole thing. And guys... there are MORE in the series. WHY. Why.<br><br>So... that was Talon. I am not taking chances on $2 books ever again, unless they have glowing reviews on goodreads. I think reading this book took years off my life, and all I wanted was a fun dragon romp.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431133134ra/14795145.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="803717861342348325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13382391382852880167" style="display:none"><u>What I THOUGHT <i>Talon</i> would have:</u><br>â¢ Epic dragon battles and wars<br>â¢ FIREBREATHING!<br>â¢ Dragon lore<br>â¢ Dragon politics<br>â¢ Awesome dragon heroine<br>â¢ Epic romance<br><br><u>What <i>Talon</i> ACTUALLY had:</u><br>â¢ Beaches, parties, the mall, boys, surfing<br>â¢ Very little action, with a super slow pace<br>â¢ Practically NO world building<br>â¢ Girl kicks guy where 'the sun don't shine'<br>â¢ Insta-love... Ugh. <br>There's going to be five books in this series. Really?!<br><br><b>

If it wasn't for her optimism, I most likely wouldn't have finished this. <br><br>I loved Julie Kagawa's <i>Iron Fey</i> series, but this just fell really flat. </span>

<div id="review_916269211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916269211" />
    <a title="Chelsea â¤Peril Pleaseâ¤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea â¤Peril Pleaseâ¤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/916269211?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea â¤Peril Pleaseâ¤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea â¤Peril Pleaseâ¤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea â¤Peril Pleaseâ¤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=alternating-pov">alternating-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer916269211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15803721678969901747"><b>
  <i>A ruse. That's all it was. Pretend to like this girl. Pretend to have feelings, to pursue some kind of relationship. Earn her friendship and trust, knowing I might have to destroy it, and her, in the end.</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Ruthless.</b> Julie Kagawa is <b>ruthless. Mad. Intoxicating...<i>Brilliant.</i></b> I just....I don't get why people aren't loving this one. Is it the content? Is it because it's about dragons and you just can't get past it? Is it the non-existent love triangle? The not-so-insta-love? Is it because it isn't </span>
  <span id="freeText15803721678969901747" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>A ruse. That's all it was. Pretend to like this girl. Pretend to have feelings, to pursue some kind of relationship. Earn her friendship and trust, knowing I might have to destroy it, and her, in the end.</i>
</b><br><br><b>Ruthless.</b> Julie Kagawa is <b>ruthless. Mad. Intoxicating...<i>Brilliant.</i></b> I just....I don't get why people aren't loving this one. Is it the content? Is it because it's about dragons and you just can't get past it? Is it the non-existent love triangle? The not-so-insta-love? Is it because it isn't over-packed like an action movie full of explosions and power-plays? Is it the <b>substance?</b> OR, is it because it isn't all about her abilities as a dragon and it focuses more on the romance? Well...see...that's the problem: <b>That's why I loved it so much.</b><br><br><b>Those eyes. I felt like they pierced right through me; that if I didn't break away now, they would peel me open to see what lay beneath. Deep within, the dragon stirred, growling. She didn't like this human, I realized. Maybe he scared her, or the intensity of his gaze reminded her of a predator. Or maybe she felt that, if I stared at him much longer, I would lose myself in those stormy eyes and forget all about a certain golden-eyed rogue, waiting for me in the darkness.</b><br><br>This story isn't about learning her abilities, about Talon itself, or even how she got to where she is now: It's about being <i>free.</i> It's about having one summer to be <i>free</i> from the system, to have fun, to not look at her past, to not face her chosen future, to <b>fall in love.</b> And, not only that, it's about <b>falling in love with <i>the enemy.</i></b> You know, that person that is sworn to kill you without batting an eyelash? That person that would soon rather stab themselves in the eye than to be in the presence of the very thing they fear and loathe more than anything in the world. I mean, how could that <i>ever</i> work? A human and a dragon? But, as they find themselves wrapped in each others' embrace, one undercover as a ploy to get close to the 'sleeper' and one <b>actually <i>being</i> said sleeper,</b> they start to wonder what it would be like to be <i>normal,</i> to stay frozen in that moment together and to never face those harsh realities and responsibilities ever again. But how could they ever be normal when they are both hiding a deadly secret-a deadly secret that could kill one another?<br><br><b>I wanted to spend more time with her; she was constantly in my thoughts, and right now the only thing I wanted was to lean in and kiss her. Which was, of course, disastrous for the mission, but I couldn't help it. Somewhere between that day on the beach when I'd met her for the first time and the night of the party when we'd kissed in the ocean, she had become something more than a potential target. She had, very inexplicably, become the most important thing in my life.<br>And that terrified me.</b><br><br>This is Julie Kagawa-Her romance is unrivaled and she embraces forbidden love like she would coddle a child. No one compares and I admire her work greatly. Kagawa is the type of writer that can suck you in without you ever intending for it to happen. She writes beautifully and has a way with words, as my friend said, erasing any remnants of the novel before that you read and loved dearly and she holds nothing back-Kagawa takes no prisoners-you <b>will</b> succumb to her writing and drown in her expertly woven pages...there is no way around it. <br><br><b>I clenched my fist around the railing, finally forcing myself to acknowledge what that meant. I'd always known, of course. It was always there, at the back of my mind; I just didn't want to think about it. But if Ember was the sleeper...I would have to kill her.</b><br><br>If it's possible, I think her writing is even better than before. This is so different from her previous novels and it really showed in this story. I didn't once feel she was drawing ideas from her previous works and nothing felt recycled. It was fresh, clean, like a whole new slate. And despite the fact that I had my doubts on whether I would like this story or not, I never once thought, 'oh, this might be a four,' or 'should I take a .5 star off?'. No, this was a five through and through-and as <i>another</i> friend said-she finally beat the 3 star book one curse! I always three star her first books in her series only to love and adore the rest of the remaining books. I am so happy with this book, it's unreal-seriously.<br><br><b>I sighed again, tipping my head back. My skin was still flushed, whether from anger or adrenaline or both, and my dragon crackled and snapped in myriad different directions. I needed to calm down. I wished I had my board. It was impossible to stay tense while floating on the surface of the ocean, its cold, dark depths lulling you to sleep. The sea was fascinating. It always amazed me how calm and peaceful it was one moment, only to bear down on you a moment later with the power and savagery of a hurricane.</b><br><br>Ember and Garret were just...so fun to follow. Maybe at first I was skeptical as to how the alternating POV would work because she's never done it before, but I loved every minute of it. I was never mad it switched to one or the other and I loved seeing the events through each of their eyes. I didn't think it was possible, but I fell in love with yet another of her male leads. Garret, for real, doll, you better watch out-I. Am. Obsesssssed with you. <br><br><b>I found myself hating him, wanting to hurt him, to drive him away from the red-haired girl who was supposed to be mine.<br>Breathless, I slumped to the wall, numb with the realization. This anger, these illogical feelings of rage and possessiveness...I was <i>jealous.</i> I was jealous of a girl I was supposed to be stalking, seducing, for the sole purpose of revealing her true nature. This had become more than an objective, more than a mission.<br>I was falling for her.</b><br><br>An undercover soldier out to kill the girl he's falling in love with??? Come on. <i>Come ooooooon.</i> How. HOT. is. that? Every look, every touch, every caress...every kiss.....I couldn't breathe. I was choking on butterflies, my heart swelled to immeasurable proportions. I was biting my lip and covering my mouth with the largest smile on my face because I couldn't contain my geek out. I don't know when or how, but he got under my skin...and every time he doubted himself or how he would ever be able to kill this girl he was holding and hoping wasn't the sleeper, my heart broke a little more...and my evil side cackled without remorse.<br><br>At certain (okay, <i>many</i>) points near the end of the story I was gasping out loud, shooting my hand up to stifle my weird sounds, chanting <i>'oh no, oh no, oh no, oh no, oh no...'</i>. I was smiling so big and then tearing up when the hard decisions had to be made. It was a roller coaster of emotions-up, then down, up, then down, thrown to the side against a massive rock and then pummeled with the ocean waves, then up again. Not once was I bored and it came to a point where this was unputdownable, because I just didn't know when that ball would drop and they would find out they were sworn enemies...and, hey, I loved those stolen kisses-I am a <i>girl,</i> after all.<br><br><b>Being with him did strange, twisty things to my insides. My dragon instincts did not approve; they still didn't like this human with his amazing reflexes and bright, intense eyes. The eyes of a predator. But there was another part of me that couldn't resist. And the thought of never seeing him again was unfathomable. Even if I knew it was probably for the best.</b><br><br>Jealousy (yaaas), lies, betrayal, true love, angst, and much more, this story became an instant favorite. The beginning was mild, I'll give you all that. But I know Kagawa, and if I know anything, she's hiding in the shadows with a malicious smile and steepled fingers because <b>the pain will come.</b> Oh, she'll bring it. I don't doubt that even for a second. I know her, and I know the end of this book was just the beginning of what we'll face in the future books. Our little Ember (on a side note, how damn cute is that name? Ember. Like a spark, a flame, a fiery soul trapped and hidden in a tiny, harmless body. So clever and fun-I love her spirit.) and my dear Garret are in for a world of trouble. I don't know what all is to come or what's up Kagawa's sleeve. But I do know one thing: She is a genius and I'll never doubt her ideas again. Because, in the end, she got me, I'm rooting for the impossible: I want that human and dragon together, damn it! <br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><br><br>***************************************************************<br><br><br><br><b>Urrrmmmmmmm....another book by Julie fuckin' Kagawa??</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Ron-Swanson-is-excited_zps2cb8d518.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077159131" />
    <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru"><img alt="Tomoe Hotaru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571221863p2/5548051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077159131?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tomoe Hotaru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tomoe Hotaru" href="/user/show/5548051-tomoe-hotaru">Tomoe Hotaru</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=zzzzzzz">zzzzzzz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=fantasy-lite">fantasy-lite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5548051-tomoe-hotaru?shelf=advanced-reader-copy">advanced-reader-copy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077159131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1755549397218647477"><i>Disclaimer: This is a review of an uncorrected Advanced Reader Copy.</i><br/><br/>Know how to ruin a potentially great fantasy novel?<br/>Cram it up to the brim with <i>Young-Adulterism</i>. That's what I'm coining this phenomena.<br/>When, at around 60 pages I'm already smacked in the face with:<br/><br/>- beautiful main characters<br/>- beautiful love interests<br/>- a <i>third party</i> making unwanted sexual advances to female MC just so male LI can step in and rescue her<br/>- a beautiful bad-boy to possibly serve as a future love-triangle<br/>- said beauti</span>
  <span id="freeText1755549397218647477" style="display:none"><i>Disclaimer: This is a review of an uncorrected Advanced Reader Copy.</i><br /><br />Know how to ruin a potentially great fantasy novel?<br />Cram it up to the brim with <i>Young-Adulterism</i>. That's what I'm coining this phenomena.<br />When, at around 60 pages I'm already smacked in the face with:<br /><br />- beautiful main characters<br />- beautiful love interests<br />- a <i>third party</i> making unwanted sexual advances to female MC just so male LI can step in and rescue her<br />- a beautiful bad-boy to possibly serve as a future love-triangle<br />- said beautiful bad-boy already demonstrating interest in female MC<br />- plus female MC seems to be ignorant of the fact that beautiful bad-boy shows interest in her<br />- the impending over-used snoozefest that is Paranormal/Fantasy-Tropes-Somehow-Forced-Into-High-School<br /><br />then you can kiss me goodbye because I'm done with you.<br /><br />Look, I know this book <i>is</i> Young Adult. But that does not mean that you have to be so <i>banal</i>. Young Adults have interests that extend beyond hot boys and teen drama, mmkay? <br />I was expecting a Young-Adult novel, focusing ON this wicked new dragonlore. Instead, it was this new dragonlore focusing on young adults. Dragons here are just used to spice up what is otherwise just your usual, <i>been-there, read-that</i> Young-Adult fluff littering the marketspace nowadays.<br /><br />So nope, ain't nobody got time for that. Pass me the next book, please.</span>

<div id="review_732595926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732595926" />
    <a title="Taschima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima"><img alt="Taschima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574541558p2/2435020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732595926?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taschima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taschima" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima">Taschima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2435020-taschima?shelf=bea-2014">bea-2014</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732595926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11634352685326115988"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415424309ra/11786673.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am a huge, huge, HUGE Julie Kagawa, fan. Her Iron Fey series as well as Blood of Eden are on my list of favorites, which is why it pains me so much to say that Talon did not deliver as I thought it was going to. It did not hook me until the very very end and by then I was looking at the Epilogue. I thought Talon focused too much of its efforts on the wrong stuff, mainly the romance and the painfully obvious love triangle. It should have focused more on world building and a more epic plotâ¦ this</span>
  <span id="freeText11634352685326115988" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415424309ra/11786673.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am a huge, huge, HUGE Julie Kagawa, fan. Her Iron Fey series as well as Blood of Eden are on my list of favorites, which is why it pains me so much to say that Talon did not deliver as I thought it was going to. It did not hook me until the very very end and by then I was looking at the Epilogue. I thought Talon focused too much of its efforts on the wrong stuff, mainly the romance and the painfully obvious love triangle. It should have focused more on world building and a more epic plotâ¦ this IS dragons we are talking about here after all.<br><br>Ember is a little dragon who just got her biggest wish granted; to spend all summer doing things she wants to do with minimal adult supervision. She will get to spend her time with her twin brother Dante, learning to ride the waves and blend in with their fellow humans. She will also get to make a lot of friends, instantly it seems, and even some enemies. But most of all, quite seriously, she will get to develop forbidden feelings for a striking human who is hiding dark secrets. Garret is of course that human, and he is tasked with the mission of finding the hatchling and putting an end to its life.<br><br>There is something about Ember that I just donât like. Yes she is adventurous, and strong, and recklessâ¦ but perhaps she is too damn reckless. At first her spirit reminded me of Rose from Vampire Academy. They are both wild and independent, but Rose has something that Ember doesnât. Maybe it is Lissa who keeps Rose grounded, or maybe it is Roseâs sense of duty that keeps her from becoming too much. Ember on the other hand doesnât have a sense of duty, and she doesnât have a Lissa. She has a twin brother, one she is supposed to be SUPER connected to but one which we barely see throughout the novel. If Ember had an anthem it would be âGirls just Wanna Have Funâ by Cyndi Lauper. Ember is just too much, and what is worst is that she is not the brightest of the bunch. She doesnât trust her own instincts and instead of questioning this random human boy who is TRYING SO DAMN HARD to get close to her and get her info all she can think is âbut well, he makes me FEEL things in my tummy!â<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415424309ra/11786674.gif" width="350" height="178" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"I felt like he was hiding so much, that I wasn't even seeing the real Garret at all, and the more I hung out with him, the more I would learn.<br>Also being with him did strange, twisty things to my insides. My dragon instincts did not approve; they still didn't like this human with his amazing reflexes and bright, intense eyes. The eyes of a predator. But there was another part of me that just couldn't resist."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415215636i/11752445.jpg" width="350" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, he looks like an enemy, talks like an enemy, behaves like the enemyâ¦ But he is just so DREAMY! LOOK AT THOSE EYES!! You can safely say me and Ember did not click. She was naÃ¯ve and gullible until the very last page. <br><br>Though to be honest Garret, the epic soldier, didn't fare much better. He should have been better at this job of infiltrating the enemy, but he was just so obvious about his awkwardness around civilians and about anything that was remotely NORMAL that I couldn't believe this girl couldn't spot his act from 10 miles away. Wake up sunshine and smell the flowers!<br><br><b>
  <i>"Startled by my own thoughts, I leaned back and rubbed my eyes. What was wrong with me? I was a soldier, trained to keep emotions in check at all times. I could face down a charging dragon and show no fear. I could endure two hours of my superior screaming in my face and feel nothing. What was it about Ember that was different?"</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415217597i/11752608._SX540_.png" width="350" height="196" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I had to choose sides in the love triangle I would have to go with Riley. He is your typical bad boy (no english accent required) but the interesting thing about him is that he wasn't just out for himself, he was taking care of many other rebels which gave him this HUGE responsibility. That made him attractive in my eyes, he is more than what his attitude may portray, he cares more than just about himself. Not that he doesn't have his moments of selfishness, but at least he is fighting for a bigger cause. Plus, he is the rogue dragon. I mean, come on, no contest.<br><br>Talon has a very obvious love triangle, and while it is not completely off-putting... I mean I get why the love triangle is there, to reflect Ember's inner struggle between her human side and her dragon side, but I would appreciate it if it would focus less on that and more on other devices because If I had to point to one thing that dragged throughout the story it would have to be the romance.<br><br>Talon was so focused on the romance that it kind of lost its edge. We only got some interesting action by the very end of the story, and even that was fairly predictable. I guess I was expecting more action and plain old <u>epicness</u> from this title and less gushy romance. I had been expecting an imaginative world and instead got the same old story only wrapped in a newish package. Maybe I am a bit disillusioned but I can still see myself picking up the sequel. I always give second chances.<br><br>OLD Update:<br><br>When I first read the news I was very excited.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380751719ra/3119512.gif" width="300" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, come on, it's Julie Kagawa!! I mean, it's dragons, and I am no fan of Dragons, but if anybody can pull it off it is most definitely her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380751719ra/3119513.gif" width="300" height="164" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As usual this woman is going to write a great story and I'm going to be all like...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380751719ra/3119514.gif" width="300" height="168" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And at the end she is going to be bathing in piles of her own money. Because everybody is going to buy this book, EVERYBODY.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380751719ra/3119515.gif" width="300" height="181" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/653873210?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=awesome-author">awesome-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=good-but-not-great">good-but-not-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-concept-poor-execution">great-concept-poor-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=loved-while-reading-but-forgettable">loved-while-reading-but-forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer653873210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5201986573217568660"><b>3.5 stars (0.5 stars for sentimental value)</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"We were taught their entire blood-filled history, from the dragonslayers, to the fanatical Templar Knights, all the way up to the militaristic order they were now... St. George was ruthless and cunning and unmerciful, the enemy of all of our kind."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Look at that passage. Just look at it. Does it not reek of potential? Does it not guarantee High Fantasy epicness in the form of dragon vs human smackdowns? Does it not promise you incredible things??<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419233573ra/13019397.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Now </span>
  <span id="freeText5201986573217568660" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars (0.5 stars for sentimental value)</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"We were taught their entire blood-filled history, from the dragonslayers, to the fanatical Templar Knights, all the way up to the militaristic order they were now... St. George was ruthless and cunning and unmerciful, the enemy of all of our kind."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Look at that passage. Just look at it. Does it not reek of potential? Does it not guarantee High Fantasy epicness in the form of dragon vs human smackdowns? Does it not promise you incredible things??<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419233573ra/13019397.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now take a look at this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I remembered the heat of [the strange dragon]'s gaze, the instant awakening of something fierce and primal inside me when our eyes met."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Those eyes. I felt like they pierced right through me; that if I didn't break away now, they would peel me open to see what lay beneath."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now imagine pages and pages of that. You start to get bored, then worried that you're bored because this is Julie-flipping-Kagawa! She penned the fantastic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6644117.The_Iron_King__The_Iron_Fey___1_" title="The Iron King (The Iron Fey, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Iron Fey</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10215349.The_Immortal_Rules__Blood_of_Eden___1_" title="The Immortal Rules (Blood of Eden, #1) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Eden</a> series and from her head, sprung a certain green-eyed, redheaded prankster that you are way too obsessed with for your own good. <br><br>But it's undeniable; your interest is waning. This was not what you signed up forâthis is Contemporary Romance bullshit, interspaced with glimpses of plot and action. It would've been fine as a 2010 Paranormal Romance, but you signed up for man-eating dragons, dammit, and you want them to fry a man's eyeballs off!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419233573ra/13019398.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then it happens. Near the end of the book when you've lost nearly all the fucks you can give: an epic dragon fight. It's intense, crazy, and exactly what you've been yearning for since you've laid eyes on that blurb. <br><br>But too little, too late. The book ends with the promise of more fights and dragon action. But nothing can redeem it from the 300+ pages of a predictable love triangle, lack of long-lasting female friendships, lackluster world-building evident by a unexplained 'magic' suit that won't rip when the MC shifts into dragon mode, and bland as tofu slice-of-life storyline.<br><br>In the end, you're left with nothing more than the sour tang of disappointment and an angry Taylor Swift gif.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419233573ra/13019399.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WHY, JULIE, WHY?<br><br><br><br><b>Pre-review:</b> I will read anything this woman writes.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429734ra/861066.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5201986573217568660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1470506532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470506532" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470506532?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21425501-talon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=romantic-recollections">romantic-recollections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470506532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10356050979063887571"><b>"The human race is weak and self-destructive, and the only thing they know how to do is destroy."</b><br/><br/>I was genuinely excited to begin this book and, judging by the synopsis, I felt it had a lot of potential. Unfortunately, I was left disappointed for a large portion of the book. The premise of a book about a teenage dragon assimilating to life amongst the human race, whilst in her human form, was intriguing, but whilst reading, this felt like more of a straight-forward romance for the most part. Rom</span>
  <span id="freeText10356050979063887571" style="display:none"><b>"The human race is weak and self-destructive, and the only thing they know how to do is destroy."</b><br /><br />I was genuinely excited to begin this book and, judging by the synopsis, I felt it had a lot of potential. Unfortunately, I was left disappointed for a large portion of the book. The premise of a book about a teenage dragon assimilating to life amongst the human race, whilst in her human form, was intriguing, but whilst reading, this felt like more of a straight-forward romance for the most part. Romance, as a main theme in novels, is ordinarily not my thing and I felt myself getting bored of all the coyness, teen angst and love at first sight. It felt like the fantastical element were almost surplus to the romantic overdose on times.<br /><br />I felt like the central portion of the novel was almost solely dedicated to an endless sea of love scenes and any forward movement in the plot was halted. The last 30% of the novel really picked up, for me, and I felt myself once more invested in the outcome of the novel. I still can't ignore that I felt like this novel could really have been halved in size and made much more impactful. <br /><br />I also disliked that the human female characters were displayed as vapid and shallow with an interest only in clothes and cute boys, and it annoyed me that there wasn't a more meaningful representative for the female human race. It seemed like all the humans, in fact, were displayed as fun-loving, talkative and easy-going. Not a bad thing, in itself, but there was a lack of deep conversation and real bonds being made beyond their love of the beach and the junk food served there. If our main character was on such an advanced level to this then why did she continue to form bonds with these air-headed individuals? I would have liked to form more of an emotional investment with the characters, but I felt it difficult when I was only given this side to them.<br /><br />I will continue with the series as I am interested to see where the novel goes but I am hesitant that it will only have more of the same superfluous love scenes and little actual plot development. This is probably due to my own personal tastes, in relation to romance novels, so please don't take this review as a verbatim portrayal of the novel. I would definitely recommend it to anyone interested in romance with a light speckling of fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10356050979063887571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it

          </div>
