        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102585743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9109819393086117514"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415833596i/11853122._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>â¸ <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1104709526' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rogue</a> â¬â¬â¬ (2.5)<br/><br/><b>Actual rating : 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>Deciding to read <i>Talon</i> was an instant-jerk reaction for me</b>. After reading a bunch of mixed reviews, I reached the decision to never, <i>ever</i> read it. Guess I was fucking wrong. Because what happened next is kind of a blur : reading Chelsea's review - downloading it - eating it - <b>loving it.</b><br/><br/>I ended to disagree with almost all the warnings I read before. <i>Go figure</i>. Maybe I'm a weirdo. <b>*shrug*</b><br/><br/><i>About what have I been warned?</i> <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Be careful, the main c</u></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9109819393086117514" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415833596i/11853122._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>â¸ <b>
  <u>Book 2</u>
</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1104709526" rel="nofollow noopener">Rogue</a> â¬â¬â¬ (2.5)<br><br><b>Actual rating : 3.5 stars</b><br><br><b>Deciding to read <i>Talon</i> was an instant-jerk reaction for me</b>. After reading a bunch of mixed reviews, I reached the decision to never, <i>ever</i> read it. Guess I was fucking wrong. Because what happened next is kind of a blur : reading Chelsea's review - downloading it - eating it - <b>loving it.</b><br><br>I ended to disagree with almost all the warnings I read before. <i>Go figure</i>. Maybe I'm a weirdo. <b>*shrug*</b><br><br><i>About what have I been warned?</i> <br><br><b>
  <u>Be careful, the main character is plain blank.</u>
</b><br><u>Here's the thing</u> : I loved <b>Ember</b> from the beginning - she was a <b>fierce and strong-minded</b> character, and I really enjoyed following her during her <i>let's try to live as humans</i> journey. Funny, sometimes over-confident but never conceited, <b>she tries to seek the truth out behind the welter of stereotypes she received since her early childhood</b>. What stereotypes? In a world, <i>Damn, the dragons are going to rule the world man!! Dragons powaaaaa!!</i><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415920329i/11865661._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"<i>All right, you bastards,</i> I though, lowering myself into a stalking position, my belly scales nearly brushing the crates. <i>We're changing the rules a bit. This time, I'm coming for you.</i>"</b><br><br>What I appreciated the most was the fact <u>she never turned a blind eye and a deaf ear to the overwhelming evidence</u> - That is to say, <b>nothing is as simple as it seems at first</b>, and humans can be pretty interesting too, <i>for a reckless two-legged animal</i>. <br><br>As for <b>Garret</b>, his journey in life appears to be utterly similar as Ember's. Except the fact he's human, he was also filled with craps at first, that is to say, the human version of world domination : <i>Let's kill dragons, they're all Evil, but we have guns, woohoo!!</i> Since the first time I met him, I was eager to see him reject this bullshit and begin to think by himself. <br><br><b>He didn't disappoint.</b> <br><br>Here's a male-lead completely <b>swoon-worthy</b>, loyal - and <b>adorably poorly adapted to the regular teenage life</b>. <i>Gah</i>, I loved him so much. <br><br><b>"A ruse. That's all it was. Pretend to like this girl. Pretend to have feelings, to pursue some kind of relationship. Earn her friendship and trust, knowing I might have to destroy it, and her, in the end.<br>It felt wrong. Dirty and underhanded, something <i>they</i> would do. But... I was a soldier, and this was my mission."</b><br><br>Do you want to know my thoughts about the second boy, <b>Riley</b>? Strangely, I really liked him too. Yes, I know, I'm stunned too - because usually, I seem to develop a strong hate toward <i>the other guy</i>, where here, well, I was pleasantly surprised to find myself laughing at his jokes and rooting for him - to a certain extent, of course, these boundaries being <i>Garret's happiness</i>. <br><br><b>"Can't <i>anyone</i> ever start a fight without all the posturing and cheesy Bond-villain threats? It's not that hard. Here, let me demonstrate." And he smashed a fist into Colin's nose."</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Be careful this is boring</u>
</b>.<br><i>Well.</i> I <i>must</i> be weird, because <b>that was such a page turner for me</b>. Go figure^^. I found <b>the plot captivating and the twists enthralling</b>, and as usual, I loved the fact the fantastic world could emerge in the real world. As I said earlier, I used to read a tons of fantasy and after almost 10 years I grew tired of learning a fucking lexicon each time I begin a new series. <i>I know, I'm such a lazy reader.</i> <br><br>While in <i>Talon</i>, the story is <b>beautifully written</b> in a way which draws us almost instantly in the life of the characters - in my case, anyway. That's true the romance overtook the plot at some point. But I don't care, because that romance? <b>Beautiful</b>. If you can't stand paranormal romance, it might annoy you though, I guess. Personally I found this first installment quite effective, even if some parts <i>were</i> predictable. <br><br><b>
  <u>Be careful there is a love triangle in it</u>
</b>. <br>When I checked reviews before taking the decision to read <i>Talon</i>, here's what made me really wary : <i>Watch out!! Love triangle hell!</i> Because as you may know, I despise them something fierce. <b>Verdict?</b> What was my surprise when I discovered <b>it wasn't a love triangle for me</b>. I know what you think : a girl, two boys? Love triangle! <i>What is she trying to say here?</i><br><br> So, let me explain : <b>I loathe it when characters - usually, the female lead - spend all their time to hang back between two boys</b>. Perfect example? America Singer. <br><br><i>Oh, I love him - But He's amazing too, you know, I'm in love with Him. What? Did I say I loved <i>him</i>? I meant Him!</i><br><br> What? What do you mean <i>Go screw yourself</i>? <br><br><b>Nothing like that in <i>Talon</i></b>. <b>Yes</b>, we have two boys. <b>Yes</b>, they're both interested in Ember. <i>Okaaaaay</i>. But for me there isn't a love triangle because what links Ember and Riley is <i>lust, attraction.</i> On Garret's side? Love. <br><br><b>"Tonight, Garret the soldier didn't exist."</b><br><br>To conclude, I have to tell you to give it a try, because some crazy people like me end loving that dragons' story Julie Kagawa delivered here. That might not be your case, but <i>come on</i>, what are six hours in a life? At worst, you'll write a rant review, and ranting is fun, right? <br><br>But if you love it like me? <b>Dammit, you'll spend an absolutely delighting moment with Ember and Garret.</b> <br>___________________________________<br>All right guys! <br><br><i>Knock knock.</i><br><br><b>Postman</b> - Hey, see, you received your copy of <i>Talon</i><br><b>Me</b> - Oh yes OMG I was <i>sooooo</i> looking forward to read it because - <br><b>Postman</b> - You know there's a public debate on it right?<br><b>Me</b> - What? No. Come on, <i>dragons</i>.<br><b>Postman</b> - Yes but you know *whisper* it seems not as good as usual. For Kagawa, I mean<br><b>Me</b> - Oh! I don't care, never read any of her books<br><b>Postman</b> - *shocked face* <br><b>Me</b> - Yes, because I've been on a fantasy break for years. There's only so much creepy elves a girl can take, you know?**<br><br>**Because I spent <i>years</i> to read only fantasy, yes, <i>years</i>, and at some point, I just couldn't enjoy it anymore without comparing and comparing with my absolute precious <i>aka</i> Robin Hobb's books - <b>yes, all of them</b>.<br><br>Actually, I downloaded it on my reader. But I <i>do</i> talk to my postman sometimes. But you saw my point, right?<br><br>Here I am, <b>Because Chelsea convinced me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916269211?ref=" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a></b><br><br><b>Ready to enter the arena!</b> TRANSFORMATION!! <i>(omg. omg. I dreamt to write this so many times)</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415654867ra/11824774.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How in the world am I not credible? Duh, that's Sailor Moon for God's sake!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9109819393086117514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText14800061475517500094" style="display:none">Actual rating 2.5 stars<br /><b>Weak and Undeveloped, but entertaining enough.</b><br /><br />It is fine, interesting. But there is something missing here.<br />The story is not all there, and the romance is too superficial. More development and connexions between the characters are needed, more deepness. <br />The characters and fantasy are feeble. The dragon part is too weak. To me, it needed to be more prevalent and powerful in the story. More fantasy. The dragon characters are puny and too human. Ember is too high-school to be believable as a dragon who grew up in a different community. <br /><br />I might give the second book a chance, but I am not very hopeful. <br /><br />P.S.:I am a bit surprised this is a Julie Kagawa's book. I looove her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228896866?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood of Eden Series</a> and it is a great contrast with what we have here.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2537360441?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Rogue (Talon #2)</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa â¥ Dog/Wolf Lover â¥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa â¥ Dog/Wolf Lover â¥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa â¥ Dog/Wolf Lover â¥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009074268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5503874779147819105"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>I thought this book was really good! I love dragons and the thought of dragon shapeshifters, so to speak, really got me stoked for this series. <br/><br/>I wasn't impressed with Ember's brother Dante, I really wished he could have been more like Ember, although she was a bit careless at times. I think you have to have the good cop / bad cop thing going on to create this particular story though. And it's not that Dante was bad, he just wanted to believe Talon and what th</span>
  <span id="freeText5503874779147819105" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br>I thought this book was really good! I love dragons and the thought of dragon shapeshifters, so to speak, really got me stoked for this series. <br><br>I wasn't impressed with Ember's brother Dante, I really wished he could have been more like Ember, although she was a bit careless at times. I think you have to have the good cop / bad cop thing going on to create this particular story though. And it's not that Dante was bad, he just wanted to believe Talon and what they stood for. <br><br>I loved the characters of Garret and Riley! Garret is in the Order, which is trying to take out all dragons. Riley is a Rogue dragon that left Talon because he knew they were full of crap. And Ember is caught up in all of this. <br><br>I loved Ember's character because she wanted nothing more than to be free to do what she wanted and to be a dragon when she wanted. She tried so hard to follow Talon's rules and listen to her brother, but when you need to be free and you know something isn't right with the group your with then you have to spread your wings and fly. (Pun intended)<br><br>In the end a few different eyes were opened from all different groups. I think/hope this is a good thing because not everyone is what they seem and it just goes to show you should never just trust in the operation/group that you are in. <br><br>I loved it and I hope I love the next book.. Rogue! <br><br>PS ~ If your looking for an epic dragon fighting book, this is not the book. There are plenty of high fantasy dragon fighting books out there and hopefully we will see more of the dragons in the next book :) <br><br><a href="http://s1379.photobucket.com/user/melmartD11/media/book%20banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437402575i/15581842._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo book banner_zpsh916lrql.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1044695819" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13250298580080357090">3.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2014/12/06/ya-weekend-talon-by-julie-kagawa/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2014/12/06/y...</a><br/><br/>I was a bit taken aback by the tepid to cool reviews Iâve been seeing for this one. Not that my own review is all that glowing, I realize, but while Talon probably wonât rank among my favorite Young Adult novels read this year, I had a lot of fun with it. By all means not a bad book. Surprisingly, most of the disappointment appears to be from fans of Julie Kagawaâs other series. Iâve never read anything else by her thoug</span>
  <span id="freeText13250298580080357090" style="display:none">3.5 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2014/12/06/ya-weekend-talon-by-julie-kagawa/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2014/12/06/y...</a><br /><br />I was a bit taken aback by the tepid to cool reviews Iâve been seeing for this one. Not that my own review is all that glowing, I realize, but while Talon probably wonât rank among my favorite Young Adult novels read this year, I had a lot of fun with it. By all means not a bad book. Surprisingly, most of the disappointment appears to be from fans of Julie Kagawaâs other series. Iâve never read anything else by her though, so thereâs really nothing for me to compare this to.<br /><br />But letâs move on to what the book is about. Talon is about dragonsâ¦but also not really. If youâre looking for a novel featuring these magnificent creatures in all their winged and scaly fire-breathing glory, youâre not going to find much of that here. What you have instead is a small group of dragonkind who spend most of their time in human form, hoping to infiltrate our society and one day take over the world again. A secret faction of dragon slayers called the Order of St. George is determined not to let that happen, and their members continue to hunt dragons like they have for time immemorial.<br /><br />The book begins as two young dragon siblings, Ember and Dante Hill travel to California in their human forms to begin training for their future positions to serve their home base of Talon. Ember is fascinated with humankind, and wants nothing more than to enjoy the summer living out the full teenager experience â beaches, arcades, ice cream parlors, the whole shebang. Her brother Dante on the other hand is a lot more disciplined, and does not like it one bit when a rogue dragon shows up in their territory, distracting Ember from her training. Meanwhile, St. George has received the rumors of new dragon recruits in the area, and the young soldier Garret Xavier Sebastian and his partner are tasked to hunt these Talon agents down and kill them.<br /><br />Encouraged to mingle and blend in with other teenagers, Ember and Dante spend most of this book as humans. But unlike other books with shape-shifting dragons (like Rachel Hartmanâs Seraphina for example, which I thought did a really good job developing the culture and world of the draconic characters), itâs difficult to think of the dragons here as anything but human. This is what I meant when I cautioned not to think of Talon too much as a âdragonâ book. Despite a few scenes of Ember thinking as a dragon and being a dragon â and they are quite few and far between â the author often seems to put her human persona before her draconic one. Plus, the setting is modern and urban. Emberâs life revolves around surfing, parties, friends and boys. Very little is known about the dragon home of Talon and Kagawa doesnât really get into it. For those craving a bit more fantasy and world building, I can see how that could cause some frustration.<br /><br />As such, this ends up being your rather typical contemporary young adult novel with a light fantasy twist, complete with love triangle and just a dash of forbidden love. Despite being exactly what I expected, it was undeniably entertaining.<br /><br />After reading this, however, I admit to being skeptical of Kagawaâs writing. Itâs obvious that she can spin a good yarn, but there were some plot elements that were so illogical and downright silly, it can be difficult to take these characters seriously. First of all, if you can take any form and youâre trying to covertly infiltrate and gain influence in human society, I would not do it as a teenager. Good luck gathering any useful information to bring back to your overlords, unless theyâre interested in how your airheaded friend thinks so-and-so is so totally gorgeous and has nice abs. Talon is also so bad at this undercover secret agent stuff, Iâm not surprised St. George managed to narrow their search down to Ember and Dante and their group of beach bum friends in like all of two seconds. Youâre a dragon spy, and youâre seriously going to stick with Ember for your name? You might as well paint a target on your back and wear a big sign that says âIâM THE DRAGON!â and hang it around your neck. The Order of St. George doesnât seem that much more competent either. At one point, Garret admits to his partner that he is getting too close to Ember and recommends stepping back from the mission. Instead of allowing Garret to do so, what does his partner do but tell him to take advantage of this new development to go even deeper into the case. Um, no! As soon as one of your soldiers gets emotionally involved and becomes compromised like that, you pull them the hell out. A lot of the problems that St. George experience near the end, they brought most of them on themselves.<br /><br />These little moments aside, not much else detracted from the experience. Yes, the story is pretty standard but ended up being more interesting than the description made it sound, and it held my attention to the end, which isnât something I can say for a lot of YA. The next book, predictably called Rogue, looks like it will delve deeper into the both the secret Order of St. George and the dragon organization Talon, so hopefully readers get the world building we want there.</span>

<div id="review_1967118892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1967118892" />
    <a title="Krystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal"><img alt="Krystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491478087p2/18989854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1967118892?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystal" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal">Krystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743566619" href="/book/show/20933811-talon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=light-fantasy">light-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=loved-up">loved-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1967118892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18291691034707688517"><b>I came here for dragons. <i>Was not disappointed.</i></b><br/><br/><u>Summary:</u> Ember and Dante are dragons disguised as humans. They are learning to act human by making friends with humans and doing <i>fun human things</i>, while doing secret dragon training on the side. Garret is a dragon-hunting human, whose latest mission involves pretending to be a normal human. He does this by making friends with humans and doing <i>fun human things.</i><br/><br/>I liked these characters. Ember is so feisty and I loved that inner fire (haha) that made he</span>
  <span id="freeText18291691034707688517" style="display:none"><b>I came here for dragons. <i>Was not disappointed.</i></b><br /><br /><u>Summary:</u> Ember and Dante are dragons disguised as humans. They are learning to act human by making friends with humans and doing <i>fun human things</i>, while doing secret dragon training on the side. Garret is a dragon-hunting human, whose latest mission involves pretending to be a normal human. He does this by making friends with humans and doing <i>fun human things.</i><br /><br />I liked these characters. Ember is so feisty and I loved that inner fire (haha) that made her so headstrong and determined to do things her own way. I liked that, even though she wasn't allowed to dragon-up, she still wasn't afraid to kick boys in the balls when they were jerks. <br /><br />Garret was a little bit too mopey and rigid but I liked when he got sassy. That little glimpse of cheekiness was <b>FUN</b>. Plus - here's a new one for me - I liked that he had 'gunmetal eyes'?? Such a ridiculous thing but I was so very attached to this description. Not that I've ever seen anyone with grey eyes in my entire life. Is this actually a real thing?<br /><br />Anyhoo. Their whole relationship is entirely predictable and full of inevitable drama, but I enjoyed it with lots of heavy sighs. They were just CUTE. <br /><br />Dante ... oh, how he disappointed me. I wanted more of him, and I wanted him to be less straight-laced. I wanted to read about him having his own fun, and being an annoying older brother, and doing stupid things ... his part in this book was incredibly underwhelming. Overall, he turned out to be a pretty dull character.<br /><br />You know who was fun though? RILEY/COBALT. Oh, hey, look - I'm keen on the bad boy again. *dramatic sigh* He was also not in it quite as much as I'd have liked, and I appreciated his edginess so he was less fun when his edges were softened, but he was fairly entertaining. I do wish he'd been a little more badass, though. More rebel, more fierce, more sassy. Oh well. I'll take what I can get.<br /><br />I enjoyed the <i>fun human things</i>, and was surprised at myself enjoying all that bloody surfing. I mean, it's just surfing. I don't get it. But they were fun interactions so okay then! I liked the group of friends, too, though I never became particularly attached. Was secretly hoping at least one of them would turn out to be a dragon.<br /><br />The book is divided into two main chunks, and the second part is where we get the most fun dragon action with teeth and claws and scales and, like I said, <b>
  <i>I came here for dragons.</i>
</b> That amped things up and made it all much more fun and entertaining. The first part is mostly boy/girl drama, which is fun but less dragon-y. I liked the action, and there was much more to be had in the second part of the book, which gives me abundant hope for the next book.<br /><br />Beyond the original idea of dragons shapeshifting into humans to fit in, there's nothing terribly unique in this book. It's very <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> with its forbidden romance, even if neither of our loved-up puppies realises; it's quite obvious that it's all a disaster waiting to happen. The characters are familiar enough, as are the events, and even the training. The rebelling against a structured society. The rebels who are actually the good guys. The oblivious friends. Not a lot that I haven't read before. But I still really enjoyed it, and I'm so glad there was still vicious dragon action because that was the 4th star for me. Without the dragon action, this is a pretty average, 3-star read.<br /><br />It's not exactly a work of genius but it <i>is</i> a fun story with likable characters and plenty of drama. I'm looking forward to reading the next book. Hopefully there'll be <b>even more dragons.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18291691034707688517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_980840201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/980840201" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980840201?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980840201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7257732581969988737"><b>That was <i>SOOOOOO</i> GOOD!</b> I really wasn't expecting to like this book because I'd heard so many mediocre reports. But I do so love dragons. I LURVE DRAGONS. And while this book isn't 100% focused on their <i>dragonish-ness</i> (totally a word) it has characters I love and sparky humour and a ship I plan to sail until dawn. <br/><br/>Where do I even begin?! GAH! Let's talk about the characters. There are 3 POVs, Ember (dragon), Garrett (dragon killer) and eventually Riley (rogue dragon). <br/><br/><b>Ember:</b> is really spunky and </span>
  <span id="freeText7257732581969988737" style="display:none"><b>That was <i>SOOOOOO</i> GOOD!</b> I really wasn't expecting to like this book because I'd heard so many mediocre reports. But I do so love dragons. I LURVE DRAGONS. And while this book isn't 100% focused on their <i>dragonish-ness</i> (totally a word) it has characters I love and sparky humour and a ship I plan to sail until dawn. <br><br>Where do I even begin?! GAH! Let's talk about the characters. There are 3 POVs, Ember (dragon), Garrett (dragon killer) and eventually Riley (rogue dragon). <br><br><b>Ember:</b> is really spunky and awesome. REFRESHING. She has a razor sharp tongue and is reckless. I totally loved her relationship with her brother and the way she gritted her teeth bared her tough training...and sneaked off to have fun. I JUST LIKED HER A LOT. Although, come on. Red hair?! Seriously? Why do all the YA heroines have red hair/green eyes these days?! And I have to admit her name is almost too cliche for me to swallow. Har, har, a DRAGON named EMBER.<br><b>Dante:</b> is Ember's twin brother and mildly adorable. He's the follow-the-rules kind of guy, but he's still a sweetie. I REALLY liked him and it was refreshing to read about a sibling relationship. Although, um, they grow apart and start being stupid at each other and Ij ust watned to smack them in the heads and say "YOU'RE A FAMILY. ACT LIKE ONE." <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I nearly diiiiied of happiness when I thought Dante was going to throw everything and just be a rogue because it meant keeping Ember safe. I LOVED HIM. And then of course, the little weasel went and tattled. I don't hate Dante, but with the epilogue saying he has to now go retrieved Ember, omg. PLOT THICKENS. I love this.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Garrett:</b> I was <i>not</i> expecting to be so into Garrett. He's like a military boy who's never had fun and is all "do the job, be the job" and duuuuuh he falls for Ember. He's not 100% sure she's a dragon though, but he does suspect. It's absolutely painful watching him try to have fun. I SHIP THEM SO HARD.<br><b>Riley:</b> Oh Riley Riley, Riley. Here is where it all falls apart. I could not care TWO HOOTS about Riley the Rogue. (At least his name alliterates. That's something.) I felt like he had zero character development and he takes Ember on a wild midnight flight at one point and then afterwards he's apparently in love with her. Um. Okay. It just felt so odd, because Garrett and Ember have this slow burn relationship that develops into something HUGE. And here's Riley just suddenly "I'm not leaving without you Ember!" And Ember swallows that?! It did NOT read like a triangle until the last 100-pages. I just thought Riley wanted recruits for his band of misfits. Plus, why do I care about Riley and the Rogues??? They're not DOING anything. They're just running around hiding. If they'd been rebels with a cause I might've gotten it. But I care 2% about them and I am really frustrated that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ember chose them over her own brother. Dante is AWESOME. Riley is DUMB. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Gah.<br><br><b>The plot is about Dante and Ember fitting into human life over a summer.</b> So they learn to mingle (hehe, that's hilarious) and go shopping and drink smoothies. It's really quite adorable. It almost reads like a summer chick-flick, but in between, there's Garrett shooting things and Dante/Ember getting trained for service in their order (called Talon). They don't spend an awful lot of time AS dragons. I didn't mind, but I get why this'd be disappointing for some people. <br><br>Also I think it was SERIOUSLY COOL that the dragon hunters are the Order of St. George. Like the story of George and the Dragon?! EKKK. I SEE WHAT YOU DID THERE, JULIE KAGAWA.<br><br><b>I loved SO MUCH OF THE BOOK.</b> From the forbidden love to the training, to the siblings, to the surfing (!!), to the pop culture references (they reference Shrek and I giggled) to my heart tugging all over the place with these characters. Riley can drop dead, of course. But GARRETT AND EMBER AND DANTE ARE SOME OF MY NEW FAVOURITE CHARACTERS. I don't usually hanker for book 2 as much, but pleeeeease someone give me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17342749.Rogue__Talon___2_" title="Rogue (Talon, #2) by Julie Kagawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Rogue</a> right now or I'm going to EXPLODE WITH FEELS. <b>The cliffhanger is strong with this one.</b> But it's definitely not unbearable. I've suffered worse. <b>An incredible scaly story....I'm SO GLAD I took a chance and read this.</b> I want to go read all the Kagawa books now...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425808733ra/13936299.gif" width="400" height="264" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7257732581969988737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QqpVEcpZoGRVBOb/39pU42xoIu0Cykg97kIK5l9arZRuKJVY8JI+IjTpYVN3igPhtrK8BXh/aQ/MunBITqW5Yg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lnWlBPsmJ/VkY4gqrZQD0HlVHkfWWHNWhDbKRgis92q692VNwe25swWOD4YFxFTSo4+Ar6ztUmSmzrDoGVPjnA==')})
  }
